## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, encompassing elastic behavior, strain hardening, and thermal softening effects typical of constitutive models in solid mechanics and metallurgy.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = c0 * (c1 - T) * epsilon (linear elastic with thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon equation for plastic strain hardening)
- Ludwik hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic with yield stress offset)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (saturating strain hardening)
- Johnson-Cook (simplified): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook homologous: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - (c3 * T)**c4) (flow stress with power-law thermal softening)
- Arrhenius-type thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * (c3 / T)) (thermally activated flow stress)
- Linear thermal softening with hardening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon) * (c2 - c3 * T) (bilinear model)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (strain hardening with exponential thermal effect)
- Swift hardening with thermal term: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (shifted power law with temperature)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2)**c3 (nonlinear elastic-plastic)
- Polynomial with temperature coupling: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon * T + c2 * epsilon**2 (cross-term model)
- Zerilli-Armstrong type: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (dislocation mechanics-based model)
- Logarithmic hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * log(1 + c2 * epsilon) * (c3 - c4 * T) (log hardening with linear thermal softening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening in metals → multiplicative factor (1 - (T/Tm)^m) or exp(-c*T) reducing stress at higher temperatures
- Strain hardening in plasticity → power-law epsilon^n with 0 < n < 1 (work hardening exponent)
- Yield stress offset → additive constant c0 representing initial yield strength before hardening term
- Thermally activated deformation → Arrhenius-type exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) reflecting dislocation mobility
- Saturation hardening → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) form reflecting dislocation density saturation at large strains
- Separable temperature-strain coupling → product form f(epsilon) * g(T) when mechanisms are independent
- Shifted strain origin → (epsilon + epsilon_0)^n to account for pre-strain or elastic-to-plastic transition
- Homologous temperature scaling → T appears normalized as (T - T_ref) or ratio form, reflecting melting point scaling
- Concavity transition in stress-strain → competing terms (hardening vs. softening) suggesting sum of power laws or rational forms
- Phase transition or mechanism change → piecewise or sigmoid-like transitions in temperature dependence around critical T
